## ⚠️ Known Issues & Gotchas

### 🔵 RLS role helpers matched auth.uid() against a DRIFTED public.users.id — 5 users failed EVERY role gate (Session 156, 2026-07-23)
`is_manager_or_above()` / `is_sr_manager_or_admin()` / `has_role()` / `is_insurance_wo_writer()` all joined `public.users` on `u.id = auth.uid()` — but andrew/mauricio/ryan/solar/tipton have a `public.users.id` that does NOT match their auth uid, so all four helpers returned FALSE for them. Symptom split that made it confusing: an RLS-blocked UPDATE **no-ops silently** (USING false → 0 rows, success response — the S141 204-gotcha), while the follow-on INSERT (WITH CHECK) throws the visible “new row violates row-level security policy”. FIXED S156 (`rls_role_helpers_email_match_s156.sql`): each helper now matches by id OR `lower(u.email) = lower(auth.jwt()->>'email')` (precedent: `is_silo_manager()` already email-matched staff). The id DRIFT itself is NOT fixed — see the 🔵 reconcile TODO. Rule of thumb: a “the save said nothing but nothing changed” report on a role-gated table → suspect RLS + this drift FIRST.

### 🔵 TCPA opt-in keywords are GATED on opted_out_at as of textly-webhook v1.2 — a bare "Yes" is just a reply (Session 155, 2026-07-22)

v1.1 treated any inbound body of exactly START/YES/UNSTOP as an opt-in and fired the "You are resubscribed..." confirmation unconditionally — so opted-IN customers answering "Yes" to a staff question got the confirmation (S154 Johnny Huddleston incident), and because keyword messages skip the notify fork, staff were never notified of the reply. v1.2 demotes opt-in keywords to a normal message unless `opted_out_at` is set. POLICY (Roland, S155): everyone in the messaging DB is opted-in by default; opt-in/out is the STOP/START lifecycle only. Consequence for future work: never add conversational words to OPT_IN_KEYWORDS without this gate, and remember STOP/HELP behavior is unchanged (STOP always opts out + confirms).

### 🔵 Supabase compute was free-era NANO until S155 — Pro includes $10/mo credits that cover Micro (Session 155, 2026-07-22)

The "exhausting multiple resources" dashboard banner was NOT workload: the project still ran on the 0.5 GB Nano instance retained from before the Pro upgrade (Nano cannot even be newly launched on paid plans). Symptoms: memory committed pinned at the limit, heavy swap, IOwait-dominated CPU, 40-65%/day disk-IO burst consumed by swap churn — while the real workload was tiny. Fixed S155: Settings -> Compute and Disk -> Micro (1 GB / 2-core), $0 net because Pro’s $10/mo compute credits fully cover Micro; ~2 min restart downtime. CAUTION for future restarts: inbound texts hitting textly-webhook during the restart window are LOST (Textable relay does not retry) — schedule compute changes outside business hours. Spend cap stays ON; disk stays 8 GB (0.43 GB used).

### 🔵 staff.role values are lowercase snake_case — and there is NO 'Admin' role (Session 154, 2026-07-22)
review-feedback's manager notify silently matched ZERO staff because it queried `.in('role', ['Manager','Sr Manager','Admin'])`. Real values: `manager` / `sr_manager` / `parts_manager` / `tech` — admins (Roland, Lynn) are `sr_manager`. Any recipient query must mirror send-dropoff-report's pattern: `['manager','sr_manager','parts_manager']` + `active !== false` + non-null email. Caught only because the live No-path test checked the DB for the queued notification — a 200 from the fn proved nothing.

### 🔵 CLOUD sessions CAN merge branches WITHOUT checkout — temp-index git plumbing (Session 153, 2026-07-22)
The S149/S150 limits (no deletes -> checkouts die; no network -> no push/clone from the bridge; REMOTE-container classifier can refuse `git clone` of this repo outright, S153) do NOT block merges. Pattern, run entirely against the mounted repo: `export GIT_INDEX_FILE=/tmp/x.idx; git read-tree -m $(git merge-base A B) A B` -> `git ls-files -u` for conflicts -> resolve via `git cat-file blob <stage-sha>` + `git merge-file` -> `git hash-object -w` + `git update-index --cacheinfo` -> `git write-tree` -> `git commit-tree $TREE -p A -p B -m msg` -> `git update-ref refs/heads/A $COMMIT`. Working tree untouched (Roland can stay checked out elsewhere), no unlinks needed. Verify/test the merged tree by `git archive $TREE > _to_delete/x.tar` -> device_stage_files -> extract + run harnesses in the cloud container. Litter rules still apply: `mv .git/*.lock _to_delete/` after every step; note EVERY bridge `git status` leaves a fresh 0-byte index.lock (harmless for reads).

### 🔵 Uncommitted context-doc edits BLOCK the pre-prod→main checkout mid-promote (Session 153)
CLAUDE_CONTEXT.md routinely differs between pre-prod and main (End-Session doc commits soak on pre-prod), so a dirty working copy of it aborts `git checkout main` mid-promote — the S153 first promote attempt half-ran (tag + feature push succeeded, main never moved; the 4-hash assert caught it exactly as designed). Fix: `git stash push -- CLAUDE_CONTEXT.md` around the main FF, and merge the EXPLICIT release hash (`git merge --ff-only <hash>`) rather than `pre-prod`, so main lands on the release commit regardless of pre-prod's tip.

### 🔴 A LONG-LIVED FEATURE BRANCH SILENTLY SHIPS RETIRED VENDOR PLUMBING — check branch currency before ANY promote (Session 152, 2026-07-21)
`feature/sidebar-layout` (branched S147) still posted to `projectblue-send`: the S152 sidebar live test sent a REAL text out the retired PB temp line (it still works!) instead of Textly. Nothing errored — the UI looked normal, the message arrived, only the sending line was wrong. Before promoting any branch older than the last release: run `git log <branch>..main --oneline`, merge pre-prod/main IN first, and grep the branch for retired endpoints (`projectblue-`, `kenect-`). Re-check version numbers at merge time too (branch says v1.477; prod is v1.480 — sidebar ships as v1.481).

### 🔵 Edit RO save writes no-op audit rows; parts add/delete never re-renders the board (Session 152, 2026-07-21)
Both found during the S152 sidebar live regression; both LAYOUT-INDEPENDENT (classic behaves the same): (1) edit-save audits unchanged fields (old==new rows, plus '18495' -> '18495.00' format-only writes); (2) partsData updates skip renderBoard, so card chips go stale until any re-render (a search jiggle fixes them), and a SECOND tab keeps boot-time partsData forever (GH#36 family — this masqueraded as a sidebar bug until a controlled repro cleared it). TODO rows added for both.

### 🔵 After-hours auto-reply architecture (textly-webhook v1.1, Session 152)
app_config keys: `business_hours` JSON `{"tz":"America/Chicago","mon":"08:30-17:00",...,"sat":null,"sun":null}` (null day = closed all day), `after_hours_reply_text`, `after_hours_reply_enabled` ('false' = kill switch; missing keys fall back to hard-coded defaults that MATCH the live config). Dedupe: ONE outbound messages row context `after_hours_auto_reply` per number since the closed period began (period start = most recent open instant via 30-min walk-back; 24h fallback if closed 8+ days). A dedupe-check DB error SKIPS the send (never risk spamming a customer all night). Testing trick: set today's day to null in business_hours, text the line, restore — but customers texting during the window get the closed reply (S152 did this with live traffic flowing; keep it SHORT).

### 🔵 Supabase JS returns at most 1000 rows by default — a `select('*')` with no `.limit()` is a SILENT window, not "all rows" (Session 151, 2026-07-21)
messages.html loadConversations() pulled `conversations` with no limit and everyone assumed "all"; the 3,225-row Kenect import blew past the PostgREST default max-rows (1000) and the inbox silently showed only the newest 1000 — New Contact's "open existing" then no-op'd on any older conversation (selectConversation couldn't find the id locally) and name/phone search missed old contacts entirely. Fixes shipped S151: selectConversation fetches the row on demand and joins the cache; search runs a debounced server-side sweep (digits→phone_key ilike, text→customer_name ilike) and merges hits; an active search OVERRIDES the status filter chips (every imported conversation is closed — the Open chip hid exactly what search must surface). AUDIT CANDIDATE: any other unlimited select on a table that can grow (repair_orders reads are fine today at ~hundreds; cashiered/messages queries all carry limits or windows — re-check when tables grow).


### 🔵 Textable (Textly) API — auth is `Bearer accountUid:accessToken`, v1/v2 split, user endpoints tenant-locked (Session 151, 2026-07-21)
API base `https://vestednetworks-txb.textable.app` (the Textly portal at textly.vestednetworks.com talks Firestore directly, NOT this REST API). Send auth: `Authorization: Bearer <firebaseUid>:<apiToken>` — the bare token alone 401s with a reason string that tells you the format. The apiToken is minted via `POST /api/v2/users/{uid}/token` with a FIREBASE bearer (read from the portal tab's IndexedDB `firebaseLocalStorageDb`, S140 pattern). BUT: v1 token mint, `POST /api/users/{id}/webhook`, and v2 self GET/PATCH all return 401/403 for Roland's user — user-level API is tenant-admin locked AND his provisioning is partial (Firestore user doc `external_id` is EMPTY, number attached as 'shared' only). The relay webhook therefore had to be set by Vested (Marcus Hayward) in their admin UI, at the SHARED-NUMBER account level (works fine — relays both directions). No message-list/status API is documented: the relay webhook is the ONLY inbound path, so anything that arrives while the relay is broken exists ONLY in the Textly console and will NOT backfill. Textable 451 on send = THEIR side opt-out. Relay payload is PascalCase (`MessageID/ToNumber/FromNumber/MessageBody/MessageDirection/ContactName`), no timestamp, no documented media field — textly-webhook parses tolerantly and logs the raw payload.

### 🔴 A URL sent by EMAIL arrives GMAIL LINK-WRAPPED — vendors paste the wrapper, not your URL (Session 151, 2026-07-21)
Marcus (Vested) set the relay webhook to what he copied from Roland's email and every relay POST silently went to google.com: Gmail had rewritten the URL to `https://www.google.com/url?q=<real-url-with-secret-%3D-encoded>&source=gmail&ust=…`. Nothing errors — the relay 'works', delivery just vanishes. When sending a webhook/callback URL to a vendor by email, tell them to paste it as PLAIN TEXT (not click-copy the link), and verify the saved value starts with YOUR host and has a literal `?secret=`. Diagnostic that caught it: our endpoint self-test (curl with a synthetic payload) returned ok:true while real relays never arrived → the fault had to be the registered URL.


### 🔵 CLOUD Cowork sessions cannot delete files — branch switches die MID-CHECKOUT; recover, don't retry (Session 149, 2026-07-21)

A session run "In the cloud" reaches the repo through the desktop device bridge, which allows create/write/rename but NOT unlink — and the S143 `allow_cowork_file_delete` tool DOES NOT EXIST there (it is local-session-only). Consequences seen live S149: (1) `git checkout pre-prod` needed to delete feature-only files, failed halfway, and left a HALF-APPLIED working tree (staged deletes + modified files) — recovered with `git show HEAD:<file> > <file>` for each touched file + `git read-tree HEAD` (writes/renames work; deletes don't). Do NOT keep retrying checkout — each attempt leaves new lock litter. (2) Stale `.git/index.lock`/`HEAD.lock` can't be rm'd but CAN be `mv`'d into `_to_delete/` (rename is permitted). (3) `scripts/backup.sh` old-snapshot pruning fails with "Operation not permitted" — cosmetic, the new snapshot still completes; `_to_delete/` and stale `.backups/` dirs need an occasional manual sweep from Terminal. Branch switches in a cloud session: have Roland run them in Terminal, or start the task "On your computer".

### 🔵 CLOUD Cowork sessions cannot `git push` either — device bridge has NO network (proxy 403); and commit leaves a live `HEAD.lock` behind (Session 150, 2026-07-21)

Extends the S149 entry above. Seen live S150: (1) `git push` from the device bridge fails with "Received HTTP code 403 from proxy after CONNECT" — the bridge VM has no network access at all, so **every push must be pasted into Roland's Terminal** (or run in an on-computer session). `git commit` works fine (object writes are creates). (2) But after a successful commit, git cannot unlink its own `HEAD.lock` ("Operation not permitted" warnings) — the lock file is LEFT IN PLACE and the next git command in ANY shell dies on it. **Immediately `mv .git/HEAD.lock _to_delete/` after every cloud-session commit.** This is also the origin of the "stale zero-byte HEAD.lock" that blocked Roland's checkout at S150 start (left by the S149 End commit). Same-family litter: `.git/objects/*/tmp_obj_*` files accumulate (harmless). File edits avoid FUSE fights entirely via SendUserFile → device_commit_files.

### 🔵 `a += await f()` LOSES updates across concurrent workers — page counters undercounted 159 vs 355 real (Session 149, 2026-07-21)

JS desugars `a += await f()` to `a = a + (await f())` — `a` is READ BEFORE the await suspends, so with N concurrent workers the increments stomp each other. The S149 delta driver's progress counters silently swallowed ~55% of message inserts (reported 159; the DB had 355). Write `const n = await f(); a += n;` instead. This is a SECOND independent way in-memory counters lie — the S141 rule stands: verify progress/results against `count(*)`, never against the extractor's own numbers.

### 🔵 requestAnimationFrame is PAUSED in background tabs — never coalesce required DOM work with rAF (Session 147, 2026-07-20)

The sidebar card-regroup pass originally coalesced via requestAnimationFrame after the boardGrid MutationObserver fired. Chrome suspends rAF callbacks for backgrounded tabs, so a freshly-rendered board silently stayed UNGROUPED until the tab was refocused — it "worked" whenever we were watching and failed whenever we were not. Fixed in js/layout.js by coalescing with setTimeout(fn, 0). Rule: rAF is for paint-synced animation only; anything that MUST run regardless of tab visibility uses setTimeout/microtasks.

### 🔵 localhost dev serves STALE module JS — page reload is NOT enough (Session 147, 2026-07-20)

Editing js/*.js under a running python http.server: a normal reload (and even location.reload() / ?cachebust on the PAGE url) still executed the OLD cached module files — js/app.js module imports keep their own URLs, so page-level cache-busting does not touch them. Symptom S147: new render.js code (data-ro-sid) absent after multiple reloads. Fix: hard reload (Cmd+Shift+R). Extends the S102/S90 GH-Pages cache gotcha to LOCAL dev.

### 🟡 sampleData placeholder ROs flash on boot; hidden in sidebar mode, still visible in classic (Session 147, 2026-07-20)

index.html ships hardcoded sampleData demo ROs (John Martinez, Robert Chen, ~line 932) rendered as a pre-auth placeholder board until the live Supabase data replaces them. Their fake overdue promised dates correctly tripped the new S147 date-trip banners -> alarming ~3s red-banner flash on every sidebar boot. Fixed FOR SIDEBAR MODE ONLY: sample cards have no Supabase uuid, so css/sidebar-layout.css hides .ro-card[data-ro-sid=""]. Classic mode still flashes sample cards + sample stats (148 avg / 162 longest) briefly — pre-existing behavior, left untouched. If it ever annoys in classic, same discriminator works.

### 🟠 Auth boot trusts a stale local Supabase session — silent 0-RV "connected" dashboard (Session 146, 2026-07-19)

Found via Lynn's iPhone. `js/auth.js` boot: if localStorage holds a session blob under `prvs_supabase_auth`, it logs "✅ Supabase session already active — skipping signInWithIdToken" and **returns without ever validating the session server-side**. A dead session ⇒ every RLS query silently returns 0 rows (post-S133 lockdown behavior, same family as the S141 "204 ≠ rows changed" gotcha): the dashboard renders, the connection badge can show, RV counts read 0 — and **no reload ever re-auths** because the blob is never replaced (killing the tab doesn't clear localStorage). Manual escape: dashboard Sign Out (runs `auth.signOut()`, clears the storageKey) or Settings → Safari → Website Data delete. Code fix (TODO'd): lightweight authenticated probe at boot (1-row `staff` select); empty/401 ⇒ force `signOut()` + fresh re-auth; also don't show the connected badge without a verified session.

**⚗️ HYPOTHESIS (unproven as of S146) — Lynn's iPhone Google sign-in:** separate issue on her device — "Google APIs timed out" in normal Safari tabs, yet `accounts.google.com/gsi/client` loads directly AND the One Tap sheet appears in a **Private** tab. Working theory: corrupted Google state under `accounts.google.com`/`google.com` in her normal browsing (site-data delete of patriotsrv.github.io alone didn't touch it). Ruled out: extensions (none), Block All Cookies (off), JS (on), network (Roland's iPhone works, same network). NOT yet confirmed — she hadn't tapped Continue in the private tab when paused. Next steps in the 🟡 TODO row.

### 🔵 GitHub Pages project path: root-relative links 404 (Session 146, 2026-07-19)

The site is served at `patriotsrv.github.io/rv-dashboard/`, so `href="/index.html"` resolves to the DOMAIN root and 404s. Always use relative links (`index.html`) in any standalone page. Bit the mockup's login-gate sign-in link; caught via web-fetch of the prod URL before the team got the link.

### 🔵 `.git/index.lock` IS clearable from the sandbox — S140's "cannot" was wrong (Session 143, 2026-07-16)

S140 recorded: *"the sandbox hit the recurring FUSE .git/index.lock blocker and cannot clear the lock itself"* and worked
around it by pushing via the GitHub API. **That is false.** S143 hit the same block (a stale 0-byte lock, no live git
process) and cleared it in one step: call the **`allow_cowork_file_delete`** tool for the folder, then `rm -f .git/index.lock`.
The FUSE mount refuses deletes *until that permission is granted* — the error is "Operation not permitted", which reads like
a hard limit and is not. Same for any other delete that fails this way (S143 also used it to remove tracked files and a 16MB
worktree). **Third guess-written-as-fact found in one session.**

### 🟠 PB number migration: three architectures, not one — and "masking" is NOT texting as your office number (Session 144, 2026-07-18)

The port conversation has been muddied because everyone (Camila, Ari, Brandie, and earlier this doc) collapsed three *different* architectures into the word "port". Pin them apart:

| | **Hosted SMS** (what Kenect does TODAY) | **Full port to PB** | **Masking** (Brandie's S144 offer) |
|---|---|---|---|
| Text AS 940-488-5047 | ✅ | ✅ | ❌ **new PB number** |
| Voice stays on Vested | ✅ | ❌ moves to PB/Twilio | ✅ |
| CSR needed | none | yes — from **VESTED**, not Kenect | none |
| VOIP group + call recording | ✅ untouched | 🔴 **at risk** | ✅ untouched |
| Known number keeps receiving texts | ✅ | ✅ | 🔴 **dies after 7/24** |

- **The current setup IS hosted SMS:** Vested = voice, Bandwidth/Kenect = SMS text-enablement on the same number. The clean like-for-like replacement is **PB text-enabling 940-488-5047 while Vested keeps voice, no port.** Brandie's "it would have to be fully ported over" *implies PB does NOT offer hosted SMS* — but that has NOT been explicitly confirmed and it is **THE question that resolves everything.** Ask it first, next session: *can PB hosted-SMS-enable 940-488-5047 without a port?*
- **CSR reality (confirmed S144):** Kenect will NOT issue a CSR — they aren't the carrier (they ride Bandwidth) and told Roland they don't know what a CSR is; they will simply DROP the number on/before 7/24. Vested confirmed a CSR is a **full-port** artifact. So: **no CSR unless Roland chooses the full port, and it comes from Vested.** PB/Camila still incorrectly expect the CSR "from Kenect" — that event will never happen; do not wait on it.
- **"Masking" ≠ what Roland asked for.** Brandie: "mask your calling number with your PB texting number" = outbound CALLS display the *new PB number*; both channels show the PB number, the real office number is hidden. You CANNOT send SMS displaying 940-488-5047 unless PB hosts it (carriers reject spoofed sender IDs). **Hidden cost nobody named:** in the masking path, after Kenect drops SMS on 7/24, inbound texts to 940-488-5047 (the number on the truck/cards/website/Google) go to a VOID. "Zero downtime" is true only for outbound-from-the-new-number.
- **7/24 does NOT strand the number** (Roland owns it, Vested hosts it) — it ends *texting* on it until PB takes over, an outage not a loss. In the masking path there's no carrier timeline at all, so the deadline on the *number* is soft.
- **The port is the CURE for the engagement gate, not just number preservation:** after cutover, customers texting the number they already know (940-488-5047) land on PB and self-engage — the only thing that fixes the 99.3% problem at scale. Every week it slips, the gate stays broken.
- **Full-port risk that got BIGGER:** 940-488-5047 is the main office line — "all calls recorded, tied to my VOIP office group." Porting it to a texting vendor to solve a texting problem risks the whole office phone setup. Don't take that risk unless hosted-SMS is a no AND a single unified number is judged worth it.
- **Call-prep questions for Brandie/Jordan (Roland requested a call S144):** (1) hosted-SMS-without-port? (2) if masking, what happens to inbound texts to 940-488-5047 after 7/24? (3) if full port, what happens to VOIP group + call recording + the OTHER office numbers? (4) engagement gate still in force either way? (yes — Camila confirmed; property of PB, not the number).

### 🔴 The Kenect import made the inbox LIE about PB engagement — 99.3% of customers are silently unreachable (Session 144, 2026-07-18)

**The most consequential finding since the migration, and it was hiding behind a stuck-queue alarm that undercounted it.**

A queue alarm reported **1** stuck text (Janine, "We've got your RV ready for pick up"). There were **2** — the second landed 15 min later and was swallowed by the alarm's own **"at most one alarm per 4 hours"** throttle. ⚠️ **That throttle means anything that sticks after an alarm fires is invisible until the next window.** The alarm is not a reliable count; query `status='queued'` directly.

**Neither was the S142 "stalls on engaged numbers" mystery. Both were the plain S138 engagement gate — and the reason nobody could see it is the S142 import.**

The engagement check that "passed" was measuring the wrong thing. Janine has 12 messages of history and no opt-out, so she reads as a warm, established customer. **Every one of those messages arrived on `+19404885047` — the KENECT line, `context='kenect_import'`. She has never texted `+19404074145`, the PB line we send from.** To Project Blue she is a total stranger. Reply-first gate → queued forever → no failure event.

| Recipient ever texted the PB line? | Moved | Stuck |
|---|---|---|
| **No** | 0 | **3** → ⚠️ **corrected to 2 usable, see below** |
| **Yes** | 52 | 0 (+3 = the separate S142 stall, since marked failed) |

🔴 **SELF-CORRECTION, same session — the "3/3" above was written before the evidence was clean, and one case was contaminated.** Roland called Janine (+17078533214): she never got the text, a re-send also failed, AND **a Kenect send to her also failed**. Her imported history explains why: **11 consecutive outbound `sent`-never-`delivered` from 2026-06-18 → 07-13, the last delivered message to her was 2024-12-18, and a Lynn reply 3 MINUTES after Janine's own 6/29 inbound was also never delivered.** Her number has been **one-way (inbound only) across BOTH platforms for ~7 months** — the fault is her number/device, not PB. **PB is exonerated for Janine; that data point is contaminated and must not be counted.**

**The thesis survives on n=2, not n=3 — say n=2.** Both survivors have *proven-good* delivery elsewhere, which is what makes them clean:
- **+19403006923 — Kenect DELIVERED 7/15, PB STUCK 7/16.** Same customer, one day apart, 3/3 delivered on Kenect. The single cleanest piece of evidence in S144.
- **+16027184932 — 22/23 delivered on Kenect, stuck on PB** (and it is PB's own support number).

**Method lesson (the S143 trap, re-sprung):** the "3/3, 100%" table was written as a heading before Janine's number was independently verified, and it read as settled fact for the rest of the session. **A denominator is a claim.** Before a stuck-message case counts as evidence against a provider, prove the number works *somewhere else* — the imported Kenect delivery history is exactly that control, and it was available the whole time.

**Silently-unreachable audit (S144) — NOT systemic; the first count was alarmist.** A raw query said "19 contacts / 39 lost messages", but **5 of the 7 contacts who had replied are TOLL-FREE (877/833/855)** — vendors and robo-texters, with staff replying "STOP" or an auto-reply firing back; toll-free routinely refuses inbound replies. That is noise. Real population ≈ **Janine + one contact last heard from in April 2025**. Check the area code before raising an alarm.

**🟠 Janine needs a phone call and an ALTERNATE contact (different number or email) on her RO — no vendor work reaches her.** She has been talking to a wall for 7 months while staff believed they were answering; the 7/13 "I understand your upset about the time…" is the visible cost.

- **Blast radius: 21 of 3,211 conversations are PB-engaged. 99.3% (3,190) are not** — and those 21 are essentially the primed staff. In practice **~zero customers can receive an outbound-first text**, and every attempt fails silently while looking successful.
- **The import didn't cause the gate; it camouflaged it.** Before S142, an empty thread was an honest signal — no history meant no history. Now every thread looks warm and none of them mean anything. **A data migration can destroy a signal that safety depended on without touching a line of the code that reads it.** Nothing about `messages` changed; what changed is what an operator infers from it.
- **The S143 🟠 row framed this as a risk arriving AT CUTOVER. That framing is wrong and it cost us.** It is live *now* — we are already on a different line from our history. Cutover doesn't create the reset; it relocates a problem we already have.
- **iMessage is exonerated as a cause:** 44/44 iMessages to engaged numbers delivered. Engagement is the predictor.
- ⚠️ **UNTESTED CELL — do not close this out until it's run:** we have never sent a **non-iMessage to a non-engaged number** (0 rows). PB routes iMessage-vs-SMS itself (`projectblue-send` reads `pbData.messageType`; we send no routing hint). If the gate is **iMessage-specific**, forcing SMS on first touch fixes everything and PB's documented "50 new outbound destinations/day" becomes true. **Decisive test: text-only send to a brand-new ANDROID number that has never texted the PB line** (Android forces SMS). Delivers ⇒ routing problem, PB is workable. Sticks ⇒ PB structurally cannot do outbound-first, and it is not a fit for a service business whose core message is "your RV is ready."
- **Roland's contradiction (S144), unresolved:** PB documents *50 new outbound destinations/day* AND *first touch must be text-only* (S130). Both stuck messages **were text-only** (`media_url` null, verified). If nothing delivers until they reply, the 50/day allowance is unreachable and describes a capability the platform does not have. **The gate itself is defensible (anti-spam). The defect is accept-then-queue-forever with no failure event** — a competent platform rejects at submit so the app can tell the user. That distinction is the strongest version of the complaint to put to PB.
- **Mitigation shipped v1.476 / messages v1.6:** `pbEngagement()` + `pbEngagementBannerHtml()` warn above the composer on both surfaces. **Warns, never blocks** — outbound-first may still be viable over SMS, and blocking would break the product on an unproven theory.
- ⚠️ **`PB_LINE_E164` in `js/config.js` MUST change at port cutover.** Getting it wrong silently inverts every engagement warning.

### 🔴 A sensor with a FALSE NEGATIVE is worse than no sensor — \b-anchor every allow token (Session 143, 2026-07-16)

Class K shipped with a bare `never` in its allow-regex. `never` matches inside **"whe-never"** — which appears in *every*
skill's "Trigger whenever Roland says..." line. So the allow-check whitelisted the entire description line and Class K
reported **"✓ No BLOCKING findings"** on a file containing a live retired-rule violation. It had run clean once and been
believed. Caught only because Roland asked for verification and the raw grep disagreed with the sensor. **Lesson: when a
sensor and a dumb grep disagree, the sensor is guilty until proven innocent.** All allow/near tokens are now `\b`-anchored;
a warning sits above `RETIRED_RULES`. A green check that is wrong does not just fail to catch the bug — it *launders* it.

### 🔴 An untested guess, once written as a heading, becomes "history" (Session 143, 2026-07-16)

The meta-lesson of S143, and the reason 3 sessions were spent chasing the wrong mount bug. S140 wrote the Known Issue
heading **"MOUNT GATE: it's a boot RACE, not a permissions fault"** — a *conclusion*, stated as fact, from an untested
hypothesis. S141 read it and believed it. S143 nearly did. The same pattern produced "the sandbox cannot clear the lock"
and "everything else in the skill stays as-is" (both also wrong, both also found this session). **This memory system is
excellent at capture and has NO mechanism for review** — nothing ever re-reads an entry and asks whether it is still true,
so confidence is preserved perfectly while evidence never catches up. **RULE: if a cause is a guess, the heading must say
`⚗️ HYPOTHESIS (unproven as of S[N])`.** Do not state it as fact until a session proves it.

### 🟠 PB queue stalls happen on ENGAGED numbers too — not just the reply-first gate (Session 142, 2026-07-16)

The S138 "engagement gate" finding is NOT the whole story. On 7/15, 4 outbound messages to +19405773777 (staff test number with extensive inbound history) stuck `queued` 18+ hrs — 3 accepted by PB (handles issued, never delivered, NO failure event) + 1 silently dedupe-dropped (no handle) — while 2 LATER sends to the SAME number delivered fine minutes after. PB's queue stalls selectively on engaged numbers and newer sends overtake older stuck ones. There is no PB-side purge or failure webhook (asked in the Jordan follow-ups, `docs/JORDAN_FOLLOWUP_QUESTIONS.md` item 1). Local handling: mark stale queued rows `failed` with an explanatory `error_message` (done S142 for the 4) — do NOT ask PB to release old stuck messages; late duplicates are worse than none. The queue-stall alarm counts `status='queued'` rows, so marking them failed also quiets it.

### 🔵 Kenect import rendering contract (Session 142)

Imported history (`messages.context='kenect_import'`) stores `media_url` entries as bare PRIVATE-bucket paths (`kenect-media/<convId>/<msgId>-<attId>.<ext>`), NOT URLs. `js/messaging.js` `_resolveMediaUrls` signs them at render (1-hr expiry) and passes https entries through. Consequences: (a) the `kenect-media` bucket must NEVER be made public and NEVER be deleted — live message rows point into it permanently; (b) any NEW surface that renders `messages.media_url` must route through `loadMessages`/`_resolveMediaUrls` or sign paths itself; (c) `loadMessages` returns the NEWEST 200 in chronological order (S142 fix) — imported threads reach 2,087 msgs, so "load older" pagination is a possible future enhancement.

### 🔴 A Supabase 204 does NOT mean rows changed — anon has no SELECT, so blind writes silently no-op (Session 141, 2026-07-15)

The single most expensive bug of the Kenect build, and it generalises well beyond Kenect. If a role has **no SELECT policy**, PostgreSQL still needs SELECT to **locate** rows for `UPDATE ... WHERE` — so the SELECT policies apply, zero rows match, and **PostgREST cheerfully returns `204 No Content`**. Nothing errors. Symptoms in S141: uploads succeeded, the extractor's own counter climbed to 1,486 files at a healthy-looking 7-8 MB/s… while Storage held **200 objects**. Because nothing was ever marked, the work-list returned the *same 200 rows* on every fetch and the pool re-downloaded them forever — the counter was measuring its own treadmill.
- **Tell:** an attempts/seen map pinned at exactly the page size (200).
- **Proof:** re-issue with `Prefer: count=exact` and read `Content-Range` → `*/0`.
- **Same root cause:** PostgREST upsert (BOTH `resolution=merge-duplicates` AND `ignore-duplicates` → 42501, since the ON CONFLICT path must read the conflicting row) and Storage `x-upsert: true`. ⇒ For a no-SELECT role: **plain INSERT only**, or a **SECURITY DEFINER RPC that returns a row count you assert on**.
- **Rule:** verify progress against the DB (`count(*)`), never against in-memory counters. Every real bug in that build was invisible in the extractor's numbers and obvious in one query. Invariant: `count(*) where downloaded=true` == `count(*) from storage.objects`.

### `DELETE FROM storage.objects` is blocked — and it rolls back your ENTIRE migration (Session 141, 2026-07-15)

Supabase's `storage.protect_delete()` trigger raises *"Direct deletion from storage tables is not allowed. Use the Storage API instead."* The SQL editor runs a script as **ONE transaction**, so a single such line silently reverted the whole teardown (it reported failure, but it's easy to assume the rest applied — it did not). Never put a storage-row delete in a migration; use the Storage API/UI. Corollary: after ANY failed script, run a follow-up query to check whether it applied *anything*.

### Storage eTags are NOT md5 for multipart uploads (Session 141, 2026-07-15)

Files over the multipart threshold (~17 MB observed) get an eTag of the form `<md5-of-md5s>-<partcount>` (note the `-2` suffix). An md5 integrity check reports these as false mismatches — fall back to comparing byte size. S141: 2 of 7,756 'mismatches' were both this, same 17.4 MB image, sizes exact ⇒ zero corruption.

### Never size a media job from one sample; and beware Chrome CDP's 45s timeout (Session 141, 2026-07-15)

Phase 0 extrapolated **2-7 GB** of Kenect media from a **single 576 KB PDF**. Reality: ~3 MB average ⇒ **~50-100 GB**, with just **78 video files at ~27 MB each ≈ half of all volume**. Roland's approval had been given on the wrong number, so the decision was re-opened → **skip video** (608 files / 8 GB), turning a ~50-hr job into ~1 hr. Related: the deepest thread was **2,087 messages** (spec assumed 327) — always page to exhaustion. Also: **CDP `Runtime.evaluate` times out at 45s but the page KEEPS RUNNING** — never retry on that timeout (it double-processes); fire-and-forget a background loop that writes progress to a global and poll it with tiny calls. And concurrency is decisive for latency-bound media pulls: 4 workers = 0.26 MB/s vs 16 workers = ~11 MB/s (3 sequential round trips per file).

### MOUNT GATE: NOT a boot race — the folder isn't attached, and the skill's path was dead (Session 143, 2026-07-16)

**This SUPERSEDES the S140 "boot RACE" diagnosis. That hypothesis was WRONG** and has now failed to help
twice (S141, S143). Three separate bugs were in play:

**1. Not a race.** S141 and S143 both tripped with the env flag reading `User selected a folder: no` and
`mnt/` holding only `outputs` + `uploads`. All 3 retries failed because there was nothing to wait *for*.
Waiting longer cannot fix "no folder attached." **Do NOT re-add waiting.**

**2. The project Context panel is NOT a session mount.** The `rv-dashboard` entry on the project page mounts
a **read-only knowledge snapshot** at `.projects/<id>/docs/` holding a STALE copy of `CLAUDE_CONTEXT.md`. It
is not the git repo. This is why the gate trips while the project page looks correct — and it is a live trap:
reading that copy IS the silent stale-read the gate exists to prevent. **Never read context from `.projects/`.**

**3. The skill hardcoded a path that does not exist.** `/mnt/rv-dashboard/` — the real bash path is
`/sessions/<session-name>/mnt/rv-dashboard/`, and `<session-name>` is regenerated every session. `/mnt/` holds
only `.virtiofs-root`. **The gate would have tripped even with the folder correctly mounted**; bug #2 was
masking this one. Resolve it dynamically, never hardcode:
`RV=$(ls -d /sessions/*/mnt/rv-dashboard 2>/dev/null | head -1)`

**Fix applied S143** (`docs/PASTE_ME_start-session-mount-fix-v2.md`): STEP 0 no longer hard-stops — it calls
`request_cowork_directory` with path `~/rv-dashboard`, which mounted in ONE call, no picker, no user action.
Stale `/mnt/rv-dashboard` paths were also purged from the skill's two reference tables and from
`SESSION_STARTER.md`. **If the gate trips again, the cause is something NEW — do not assume a race.**

> ⚠️ **The trap that was hiding here (S140, and it had a twin):** the skill's STEP 1 *still said* "If the
> workspace is unavailable, fetch both from GitHub" — **the exact silent fallback the S136 MOUNT GATE exists
> to forbid.** The skill and `CLAUDE_CONTEXT.md` contradicted each other, and only the context file was
> holding the line. Had a session followed the skill's wording, it would have read **stale context from
> GitHub** and could have clobbered newer local work. Removed from the skill S140 — but the identical
> fallback survived in `SESSION_STARTER.md` until **S143** found and removed it. Lesson: when a rule is
> retired, grep the whole repo for its twins.
> **Lesson: when a rule is added to `CLAUDE_CONTEXT.md`, check the SKILLS for contradicting text too.**
> 🔴 GitHub is a **write-backup, NOT a read source.** Retrying the mount is fine; substituting a source is not.

### 🔴 Kenect API: send NO credentials, and DON'T chase the token in-page (Session 140, 2026-07-15) — SUPERSEDES the S139 entry below

Phase 0 of the Kenect rescue proved the S139 recon entry (immediately below) **wrong on four counts**. Full
detail in `docs/specs/KENECT_EXTRACTION_SPEC.md` §0b. The traps, in the order they bite:

1. **`credentials:'include'` breaks EVERY call.** This — not a missing header — is what makes calls die as a
   bare `TypeError: Failed to fetch` (CORS-shaped, not a 401). Wildcard ACAO + credentials ⇒ browser blocks it.
   **Send no credentials.** Working header set is just `accept`, `authorization: Bearer <jwt>`,
   `x-kenect-calling-service: Web:1.2710.0`. With that, calls return **200**.
2. **The header value is `Web:1.2710.0`, NOT `web`.**
3. **You CANNOT lift the token by patching the page.** The app fires authenticated HTTP only during initial
   page load (before any injectable hook), then serves everything from cache/websocket — so no live
   main-thread call ever carries the token again. Patching `fetch` / `XHR.setRequestHeader` / `Headers` /
   `Request` post-load captures **nothing** (S140 burned ~30 tool calls proving this). The S139 advice to
   "monkey-patch setRequestHeader and grab it off the next real call" **does not work.** Do not retry it.
4. ✅ **Instead: mint your own tokens.** Kenect auth is **Firebase**. The refresh token + apiKey sit in
   IndexedDB → db `firebaseLocalStorageDb`, store `firebaseLocalStorage`, key
   `firebase:authUser:<apiKey>:[DEFAULT]` → `value.stsTokenManager.refreshToken`
   (apiKey `AIzaSyBg_fQbY56_USy3VpGWOWDGrY5qhTPFJ_k`, userId `130333`). JWT lives exactly **1 hour**. Refresh:
   `POST https://securetoken.googleapis.com/v1/token?key=<apiKey>` body
   `grant_type=refresh_token&refresh_token=<rt>` → fresh `id_token`. **Verified working S140** — the extractor
   self-renews and runs unattended. Roland only needs to be logged into Kenect in Chrome.

**Also:** contacts paginate by `offset`/`limit` **in the POST body** — query `page`/`pageSize` are *silently
ignored* and return the same 100 rows at HTTP 200, so a naive page loop yields **garbage counts** (it "found"
20,000 contacts; the real number is **3,093**). There is no `totalRecords`. And `attachments[]` has **no URL** —
only `{id,name,md5,contentType,size,...}` — so the media download endpoint is still unknown (blocks Phase 3).
🔒 Token + refresh token are credentials — never commit them.

### ~~Kenect internal-API auth: BOTH headers required, or every call dies~~ (Session 139) — ⚠️ SUPERSEDED S140, see above; retained for history only. Its `withCredentials`, `web` header value, and monkey-patch guidance are all WRONG.

Recon for the Kenect data rescue (`docs/specs/KENECT_EXTRACTION_SPEC.md`). The app.kenect.com SPA attaches
**two** headers to every data call — `Authorization: Bearer <~981-char JWT>` **and** `X-Kenect-Calling-Service: web`
(plus `Accept`/`Content-Type: application/json`, `withCredentials`). Replaying a request with cookies alone,
or with only one of the two headers, fails as a bare `TypeError: Failed to fetch` / `neterr` — a **CORS-shaped
error, NOT a 401**, so it reads like a network/permissions problem and sends you hunting in the wrong direction.
The token is NOT in the `auth` localStorage key (that holds only `getUserFeaturesError`/`pathAfterLogin`/`showOnboarding`)
— it lives in an httpOnly cookie / masked storage. **Do not go hunting for the token value.** The working pattern:
monkey-patch `XMLHttpRequest.prototype.setRequestHeader` to grab the app's OWN `Authorization` value off its next
real call, then reuse it — the token is read in-page and never leaves the browser. Also note these calls are **XHR,
not fetch** — a fetch-only capture hook returns an empty `{}` and looks like nothing is happening. Hook BOTH.
JWT is session-bound and may rotate: re-grab periodically across a long run.

### PB delivery gotchas: engagement gate + 1-hour duplicate dedupe (Session 138, 2026-07-15)

TWO silent Project Blue behaviors found in live testing, BOTH invisible to our API layer (send returns success, message just never arrives):
(1) **Engagement gate** — outbound to a phone with NO inbound history on our line sits in PB's queue indefinitely (status stuck queued). The moment the recipient texts the line ONCE, new outbound delivers instantly (stuck ones may never release). This is why ALL staff must text 940-407-4145 once before SMS notifies reach them (17/18 primed S138; Tipton pending) — and it is an OPEN QUESTION how first-contact texts to new customers are supposed to work (Jordan follow-up #1).
(2) **Duplicate-payload dedupe** — identical body + same recipient within ~1 hour is silently dropped (the swallowed send never gets a pbm_ handle; that is the tell). Automated notify bodies must vary — assign SMS is time-stamped as of messages v1.3. Keep this in mind for ANY future automated send.

### STOP gate lives on conversations; staff.phone_number is the staff SMS column (Session 138, 2026-07-15)

`conversations.opted_out_at` (by digits-only last-10 `phone_key`) is the TCPA suppression flag: projectblue-send returns 403 for customer sends while it is set — but contexts `staff_notify` and `auto_reply` BYPASS the gate (staff phones aren't customers; the STOP confirmation must go out). Any future send path MUST route through projectblue-send (or replicate the gate) — never call the PB API directly for customer texts. Staff SMS notifies use `staff.phone_number` (E.164; NULL = silently skipped) — the spec's proposed `staff.mobile_phone` was never created. Also: if a staff member's phone equals a customer phone (self-tests), staff_notify SMS rows appear inside that customer's thread — cosmetic, self-test-only.

### "Recently-Xed" reports must window on the DOMAIN date column, not `updated_at` (Session 135, 2026-07-08)
Any report/query that means "recently <verb>ed" must filter on the domain date column (e.g. `parts.date_received`), NOT `updated_at`. The S115 `set_updated_at` trigger — and on `parts`, TWO more redundant `updated_at` triggers — bump `updated_at` on EVERY update, so a row edited long after the event re-surfaces in a `updated_at`-based window. This is exactly why `send-parts-report`'s "CAME IN — RECEIVE THEM" box showed week-old Received parts (Todd Lintzen: received 7/01 + 6/22, edited 7/07). Fixed in edge fn v1.11 (window on `date_received`, bounded yesterday..today) + NEW `trg_stamp_date_received` trigger that stamps `date_received` at receive-time (the quick Received button never set it; 116/225 rows had NULL). Watch the manager + admin reports for the same `updated_at` anti-pattern. See memory `reference_updated_at_window_gotcha`. **Follow-up (🔵 off-hours TODO):** `parts` has 3 redundant `updated_at` triggers (`parts_updated_at`, `parts_updated_at_trigger`, `trg_set_updated_at`) — consolidate to one.

### PB list API + reconciliation gotchas (Session 132, 2026-07-04)
(1) `/get-messages-api` **limit max = 100** (400 error above; pagination needed only if volume grows past ~100 msgs/day). (2) List rows are **snake_case** (`message_handle`, `from_number`, `to_number`, `created_at`, `sent_at`, `media_attachment_url`) and carry **`service`** (values iMessage/SMS) — NOT `messageType` like the send response. (3) **PB list `status` LAGS reality**: the 7/4 8:21 AM send delivered to the handset on time but PB reported `pending` for ~6 hrs before flipping to `delivered` — so the stale-pending alarm (projectblue-reconcile, 30 min) can false-positive; it has a 4-hr cooldown and the threshold is one constant. PB `delivered` still only means left-their-queue — reconcile maps it to our `sent`, NEVER our `delivered`. (4) Inbound routing lives in BOTH projectblue-webhook v1.1 AND projectblue-reconcile (backfill path) — keep the matcher + notify logic in sync if either changes (same for the REPAIR_TYPE_TO_SILO copies). (5) `scheduled_notifications.source` CHECK now includes `inbound_message_notify` + `stale_message_alarm`; any new source needs another CHECK-widen migration. (6) pg_cron jobid 14 = projectblue-reconcile every 15 min (verify via cron.job_run_details + net._http_response, not job existence).

### PB messaging build gotchas (Session 131, 2026-07-04)
(1) PB dedupes IDENTICAL send payloads ~1 hour — automated senders MUST vary the body (RO code/timestamp) or a legit second send is silently swallowed. (2) PB webhooks: single attempt, NO retries, NO signature — our `projectblue-webhook` authenticates via `?secret=` (PROJECTBLUE_WEBHOOK_SECRET) and must always 200 fast; a reconciliation poll of `/get-messages-api` is the planned source of truth (NOT yet built). (3) `/send-api-message` returns NO message id — projectblue-send captures `message_handle` via a post-send poll (best-effort; can be null). (4) The webhook's outbound events are deduped against recent outbound `messages` rows so dashboard sends don't double-log — sends made from the PB web app DO get logged. (5) Rate limits: ~15 sends/10min/line — pace future EOD digest runs. (6) Post-deploy, browsers can pair fresh index.html with a stale cached js/app.js for up to ~10 min (v1.470 saw `openMessagesModal is not defined`) — new-module buttons are dead in that window; hard-refresh fixes.

### Project Blue "delivered" status is NOT a real-time handset receipt (Session 130, 2026-07-03)
During the GH#39 PB PoC, outbound from the fresh line +1 940 407-4145 reported `status:"delivered"` while messages took 4+ hours to actually reach handsets (they eventually backfilled — delayed, not dropped; root cause unexplained). Do NOT treat PB delivery status as a handset receipt for automation, and expect fresh/newly-ported lines to need a warm-up period. Also: PB blocks MMS/rich media to a contact until that contact has replied once (first-touch must be text-only). Full validation matrix + vendor Q&A: `research/projectblue_requirements.md`.

### RO key-date calendar events are SERVER-SIDE now (sync-ro-calendar edge fn, refresh token) (Session 129, 2026-07-01)
As of v1.469, drop-off/promised/pickup all-day team-calendar events are written by the `sync-ro-calendar` edge fn (single source of truth), called from `js/ro-crud.js` `_syncROCalendarServer` (create+edit) and `customer-checkin.html` v1.15. The client-side `scheduling.js` `syncKeyDateCalendars` is NO LONGER CALLED from ro-crud (left in place, inert) — do NOT re-wire it or you'll double-write. Auth is an **OAuth refresh token, NOT a service account** (org policy `iam.disableServiceAccountKeyCreation` blocks SA keys; Roland lacks Org Policy Admin). GCP project `rv-dashboard-488919`; OAuth client `prvs-calendar-server`; OAuth app was made **Internal** (External+Testing expires refresh tokens in 7 days). Secrets: `GCAL_CLIENT_ID`/`GCAL_CLIENT_SECRET`/`GCAL_REFRESH_TOKEN` (+ reused `PRVS_FUNCTION_SECRET`). Edge fn reads the 8-silo calendar map from `app_config` (keys `calendar_id_<normalized>`) with a hardcoded fallback, mirroring the app's getCalendarId. GOTCHA: `repair_orders` phone column is `phone` (NOT customer_phone) — the first cut used customer_phone and 500'd. The manual 📅 Schedule modal still creates its OWN separate TIMED drop-off appointment (not in cal_event_ids). Deploy: `supabase functions deploy sync-ro-calendar --project-ref axfejhudchdejoiwaetq`. Test via curl with the anon Bearer + X-PRVS-Secret + {ro_id}. Full detail in memory `reference_server_side_calendar_sync`.

### Manager Daily Report card layout + Fire Watch P2 behavior (Session 126, 2026-06-26)
`send-manager-report` is now **v2.4-P2c** (deployed live; cron jobid 5 fires it 7 AM CDT weekdays in send mode). Card section order is **reminders -> scorecard -> active work -> Fire Watch -> P&L Readiness -> parts -> Idle** (Idle deliberately at the BOTTOM — Roland). Fire Watch flags: F1 (promised due/overdue 🔴), F2 (promised <=3 days + no tech time in 3 work days 🟠), F3 (part past ETA + promised near-term 🔴 — **F3 SUPERSEDES F4 for the same RO**, so don't expect both), F4 (part past ETA 🟠), F5 (ordered >3 business days, no ETA 🟠); they sort critical->warning->watch. **F8 aging-tech-done is NOT a fire — it lives in P&L Readiness R9** (don't re-add it to Fire Watch). **Weekend/Monday escalation only renders on a Monday run** (`isMondayRun`) — testing any other weekday will never show "(rolled over the weekend)"; that is correct, not a bug. Consts `FIRE_PROMISED_SOON_DAYS=3` (calendar days), `FIRE_STALE_BUSINESS_DAYS=3` (business days). The Fire Watch / P&L Readiness / Idle headers carry plain-language lines that link `guide.html#rb-firewatch` / `#rb-readiness` / `#rb-idle` — those anchors are part of the guide-anchor CONTRACT.

### NEVER hand Roland an unguarded ER status-change SQL — a bare multi-statement close-out mass-corrupted enhancement_requests (Session 125 incident, 2026-06-26)
A two-statement ER close-out (`UPDATE enhancement_requests SET status='done', completion_notes=..., test_steps=... WHERE id='X' AND status <> 'done';` x2, pasted into the Supabase SQL editor) executed with NO effective WHERE on the second statement — it set status='done' + the WO-reorder completion_notes on **ALL 59 rows**. That fired `trg_notify_er_completion` for every transition into `done`, sending **~13 wrong "your request is live" emails** to requesters (12:56 UTC), and **overwrote the completion_notes** of ~23 historically-completed ERs. The editor reported "Success" with no error. Root cause: on a copy-pasted multi-statement UPDATE the `WHERE` was dropped/mangled and silently became a full-table write. **Recovery that worked (all run by Roland, verified read-only by me):** identify corrupted rows by the WO-note signature (`completion_notes LIKE 'In the Build/Edit Work Order form%'`) + the 12:56 `completion_emailed_at` stamps; revert wrongly-flipped rows to their pre-state (unreviewed/in-progress/declined) in small `id IN (...)` UPDATEs **each carrying a redundant blast-radius guard** (`completion_emailed_at >= '...12:50'` and/or the WO-note LIKE) so a dropped predicate can't nuke the table; reconstruct lost completion_notes from the INTACT `description` (admin_notes were only appended-to, never overwritten — so each ER's original request text survived) + version history; add `RETURNING id` to every write so the editor shows exactly which rows changed. **RULES going forward:** (1) every data-changing SQL handed over = a SINGLE guarded statement with an explicit `id IN (...)` PLUS a second redundant guard column; (2) always append `RETURNING id` and check the returned count before trusting it; (3) never trust "Success. No rows returned." (4) Remember flipping an ER into `done` emails the requester, so a mass mis-flip = mass mis-email. Recovery notes: PITR is an UNenabled Supabase add-on here; daily scheduled backups exist (e.g. 04:14 UTC) but "Restore" is whole-DB in-place (would lose the workday's live data); "Restore to new project (BETA)" can clone to a throwaway project for an exact table-level copy-back, but we declined it for low-value historical notes on closed ERs. (Memory: [[feedback_guard_er_status_sql]].)

### NEVER schedule an autonomous sandbox-git PROD promotion for PRVS (Session 124 incident, 2026-06-25)
A scheduled one-time task set to FF pre-prod -> main + tag + regression FIRED at its trigger time and ran git **in the sandbox** against the Mac repo's `.git` (the sandbox mounts it via FUSE). It collided with stale `.lock` files it could not remove ("Operation not permitted"), half-completed the fast-forward, and left: HEAD parked on `main`, a dirty working tree (pre-prod content sitting on old main), and a `v1.461` tag created AND pushed onto the WRONG commit (old prod `e69b4f6` instead of the release `e927270`). **Production was not corrupted** (origin/main stayed at the last-good commit) but the promotion did not complete. Two compounding causes: (a) sandbox git against the FUSE-shared repo cannot manage lock files and clashes with the Mac's git; (b) the task was disabled at 5:38 for a 5:15 fireAt — disabling AFTER the trigger time does nothing. **Recovery that worked:** on the Mac, `rm -f .git/*.lock .git/refs/**/*.lock`; confirm `git diff origin/pre-prod` is empty (nothing lost); `git reset --hard origin/pre-prod` while on main (a clean FF since old main is an ancestor); `git push origin main`; `git tag -d v1.461 && git push origin :refs/tags/v1.461`; recreate `git tag v1.461 <correct-sha> && git push origin v1.461`; verify the four-hash Sync Gate. **RULE:** PRVS prod promotions are INTERACTIVE (Roland runs git on the Mac, Claude does the Chrome regression). A scheduled task may only NOTIFY/remind — never execute git itself. If one is ever scheduled, cancel it well BEFORE its trigger time. (Memory: [[feedback_no_scheduled_sandbox_git_prvs]].)

### Supabase is removing default public-schema Data API grants — new tables after 2026-10-30 need explicit GRANT (Session 124, 2026-06-25)
Supabase email (2026-06-25): new `public` tables will no longer be auto-exposed to the Data API (PostgREST/GraphQL/supabase-js via anon + authenticated). New projects: 2026-05-30. Existing projects (PRVS, ref axfejhudchdejoiwaetq): enforced on NEW tables 2026-10-30. **Existing PRVS tables are unaffected.** The risk: the project's table-creation migrations set up RLS policies ONLY and rely on the default auto-grant (e.g. `woosender_leads.sql` has `enable row level security` + `create policy` but NO `grant`). A table created with that pattern AFTER 2026-10-30 will return permission-denied despite correct RLS. **FIX (adopt now, harmless before the deadline):** add `grant select, insert, update, delete on public.<table> to authenticated;` (+ `grant select ... to anon;` only if a page reads with the anon key) to every new-table migration. `service_role` (edge fns) is unaffected. Next table-creating work (messaging-automation P1 notification_queue/message_templates) should include the grants. (Memory: [[reference_supabase_public_grant_change]].)

### WooSender lead intake is LIVE — capture edge fn + admin review queue (Session 123, 2026-06-24)
WooSender Won-stage leads flow in via the dev's Zapier outbound webhook (Webhooks-by-Zapier POST, **custom header, NOT Basic Auth**) -> the `woosender-intake` edge fn -> the `woosender_leads` review-queue table -> the admin-only `leads.html` page. Key facts for next session: (1) the webhook auth is a SHARED SECRET — header `x-prvs-webhook-secret` must equal the `WOOSENDER_WEBHOOK_SECRET` edge-fn secret (set via `supabase secrets set`); a missing/wrong secret returns 401 with no DB row. (2) The WooSender JSON envelope is **identical across pipelines** — the same keys every time; lean lead forms just send empty strings (extraction maps "" -> null). The service/silo is derived from `opportunity.pipeline` (roof->Roof, solar->Solar), NOT the often-empty `clientServiceNeeds`. (3) `woosender_id` = `contactGuid` (stable per-lead key, present even on lean forms) is used for re-fire idempotency. (4) `review_status` CHECK = new/promoted/merged/dismissed/duplicate (the `merged` value was added by a follow-up ALTER; constraint `woosender_leads_review_status_check`). (5) `leads.html` is **admin-only** (`isAdmin()` gate) and reaches the live DB — Promote creates a REAL RO and Merge updates a REAL RO + adds a `customer_comm` note (the call transcript lands in the RO's 💬 Customer Comm section). (6) The phone dedupe matches digits-only (repair_orders phones are stored in mixed formats like `(916) 240-1344`). To extend the mapping when new pipelines appear, look at `raw_payload` first — do not assume field names. (7) **RLS needs BOTH a SELECT and an UPDATE policy** — the original migration shipped SELECT-only, so Promote/Merge/Dismiss (authenticated UPDATEs from leads.html) silently matched 0 rows with NO error and the lead never left the queue (RO updated fine because repair_orders has its own update policy). Fixed S123 by adding `"Authenticated can update woosender_leads"` (for update, to authenticated, using true / with check true; admin-gated at the app layer). LESSON: an RLS table the dashboard WRITES to needs a matching write policy; a missing one fails silently (0 rows, no error). **NEXT (top after-hours TODO):** add a dashboard link to leads.html (touches index.html).

### A from-scratch redesign stylesheet CANNOT be layered onto the legacy dashboard DOM (Session 122, 2026-06-21)
`design/dashboard.draft.css` uses generic selectors (`body`, `h1`, `.card`, `.badge`, `.stat`, a global `*` reset) written for the NEW prototype markup. Linking it AFTER `css/dashboard.css` on a copy of production (the `index.draft.html` experiment) made the page unreadable/unusable — the generic rules clobber the live DOM, which has a different structure/class set. The redesign is being pursued as a STANDALONE page (`design/board-live.html`) that fetches live data via the anon key, NOT by layering. Port to index.html only at the very end, as a deliberate full markup+CSS swap. RELATED GOTCHA: RLS policy `Anon can read repair_orders` = `using true`, so a browser CAN SELECT repair_orders with just the public anon key — no auth needed for read-only views (writes still require authenticated). Useful for standalone read-only previews/tools.

### To RE-SEND an ER completion email, reset completion_emailed_at AND re-flip status into done (Session 120, 2026-06-21)
`trg_notify_er_completion` only fires when `NEW.status='done' AND OLD.status IS DISTINCT FROM 'done' AND completion_emailed_at IS NULL`. So a plain UPDATE of completion_notes on an already-done ER does NOT re-email. To send a corrected/follow-up completion email: (1) `UPDATE ... SET status='in-progress', completion_emailed_at=null, completion_notes=...` then (2) `UPDATE ... SET status='done'`. The two-step makes OLD.status distinct from done with a null stamp, so the trigger re-fires and the edge fn reads the fresh completion_notes/test_steps at send time. Used S120 to re-send Lynn's 1aeb3f58 note (it sends a SECOND email, which is expected).

### "Off Lot - Returning" RO status is hardcoded in ~7 places — keep them in sync (Session 120, 2026-06-21)
The S120 status add (ER dac9fdda) had to touch every hardcoded status list: the index.html form `<select name="status">`, the status filter buttons, BOTH render.js card status dropdowns (compact ~L239 + standard ~L407), STATUS_PROGRESS_MAP (config.js + the inline copy in index.html ~L1204), and the ES translation map (config.js + inline ~L4038). It is also EXCLUDED from the on-lot count (render.js onLotCount, physically away) and given a statusColorMap accent (#0ea5e9). NOTE: its CSS slug `off-lot---returning` has no `.status-dropdown.status-*` rule, so the dropdown uses default tint (cosmetic only). Any future status add must hit all of these; grep `Waiting for QA/QC` to find every list.

### scheduled_notifications.source CHECK now allows `service_added_notify` (Session 120, 2026-06-21)
Migration `service_added_notify_source.sql` widened the CHECK to `manual, auto_dropoff_reminder, auto_promised_reminder, auto_pickup_reminder, service_added_notify`. The new source is used by work-orders.js addServiceToRO (ER 9b823d25) to queue a heads-up email to the newly-added silo's manager(s), sent by the every-15-min process-scheduled-notifications cron. ### work-list.js silo tag uses curly quotes (pre-existing, NOT introduced S120)
`js/work-list.js` ~line 298 builds the siloTag with curly double-quotes inside the inline `style=` attribute instead of straight quotes, which breaks that tag's styling. Spotted during the fd6c122d touch-drag work and left untouched for scope. Logged as a 🔵 TODO.

### `scheduled_notifications.source` has a CHECK constraint — widen it before adding a new source (Session 119, 2026-06-20)
Adding a new auto-reminder source SILENTLY fails the insert if the value is not in the CHECK. S119's Key Dates P3 reminders threw `violates check constraint "scheduled_notifications_source_check"` because the constraint was `('manual','auto_dropoff_reminder')` only — and the insert was wrapped in a DEBUG-gated try/catch, so it failed invisibly (promised_date saved but no reminder rows). Migration `key_dates_reminder_sources.sql` widened it to add `auto_promised_reminder` + `auto_pickup_reminder`. Lesson (same family as the parts_status CHECK): probe `pg_get_constraintdef` before inserting enum-like values, and remember `warn()` is DEBUG-gated so swallowed errors don't print.

### The ER completion-email trigger is LIVE in prod — marking an ER 'done' emails the requester (Session 119, 2026-06-20)
`trg_notify_er_completion` (AFTER UPDATE on enhancement_requests) fires `send-er-completion` (pg_net + vault `service_role_key`) on the transition INTO status='done', once (guarded by `completion_emailed_at`). So flipping an ER to Done now emails `submitted_by` what-was-done (`completion_notes`) + how-to-test (`test_steps`). Author those two textareas on the ER admin card BEFORE marking Done (updateERStatus captures them atomically; or use Save details first). If notes are blank it still sends a generic "your request is live" notice. To re-send, the row must transition done->other->done (or clear completion_emailed_at + re-fire the fn). DB-trigger->edge-fn via `net.http_post` + `vault.decrypted_secrets where name='service_role_key'` is the reusable pattern (mirrors the cron jobs; fires post-commit).

### Manager Daily Report admin COMBINED copy gets clipped by Gmail (Session 119, 2026-06-20)
The admin preview/copy renders all 9 manager cards in one email and exceeds Gmail's ~102KB clip threshold — Gmail shows "[Message clipped] … View entire message", so cards below ~Mauricio are hidden unless you expand. This is ONLY the admin combined copy; each manager's own daily send contains a single card and is not clipped. If it becomes annoying, trim the admin copy (e.g. summary-table + shop box only, or collapse cards). The new "Your Scheduled Reminders" section is forward-looking (today -> end of next week); overdue promised dates stay in Fire Watch by design.

### Check-in "duplicate ROs + RAFs not sending" = suspect a STALE CACHED kiosk page FIRST (Session 118, 2026-06-20)
When staff report both symptoms together, check the version badge at the bottom of the check-in page ON THE DEVICE before touching code. A cached **v1.10** produces both: the pre-v1.11 `getSignatureDataURL` typo aborted every RAF, and pre-v1.12 had no dup-RO guard. No service worker, so a long-open kiosk tab never re-fetches — the GitHub Pages server can be current while the device runs old JS. v1.13 hardened the dedupe to a submit-time phone/email lookup so duplicates can't happen even on a current page when staff skip the search. If RAFs still fail after the device shows v1.13, it's the inbox (RAF goes to the customer email + info@ CC, not repair@).

`repair_orders.key_status` (keys / no_keys / keypad), `keypad_code`, `keep_plugged_in` added v1.458 (migration `keys_power_fields.sql`). key_status is intentionally free text (no CHECK) so new values never need a migration — the app constrains the options.
